System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment L-R, cost function: 0
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 3 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 3 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-L-R-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
Supposing that you choose route O-L-R-D, 3 other drivers choose route O-L-D, and 14 additional drivers choose route O-R-D.
Then, your total travel cost for that period is equal to (10 x 4) + 0 + (10 x 14) = 180.
Note that in this example, 4 drivers (including you) traveled on the segment O-L and 14 drivers (again, including you) traveled the segment R-D to go from O to D.
Each of the 3 drivers choosing route O-L-D will be charged a travel cost of (10 x 4) + 210 = 250.
Each of the 14 drivers choosing the route O-R-D will be charged a travel cost of 210 + (10 x 14) = 350.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```


Human: The available routes are: O-L-D, O-L-R-D, O-R-D.
Think step-by-step before making your decision.

LLM Output: To determine the best route choice, we need to evaluate each route based on the potential cost, and hence the payoff associated with each choice, keeping in mind the goal of minimizing travel costs.

1. **Route O-L-D:**
   - Cost = 10X + 210
   - The cost is dependent on the number of participants (X) choosing the segment O-L. 
   - This route is directly influenced by the number of other drivers choosing O-L, thus it could be potentially high if many choose this segment.

2. **Route O-L-R-D:**
   - Cost = 10X + 0 + 10Y
   - The cost on this route depends on the number of participants on both segments O-L (10X) and R-D (10Y).
   - This adds another layer of variability as it depends on the number of participants on two segments.

3. **Route O-R-D:**
   - Cost = 210 + 10Y
   - The cost on this route is fixed at 210 for the O-R segment, plus a variable cost 10Y.

**Analysis:**
- Route O-L-D: 
  - If many people choose the variable segment O-L, the cost can quickly rise, making it a costly option.
  
- Route O-L-R-D:
  - It includes two variable segments, though the middle segment L-R costs nothing. This route's cost can be unpredictable as it depends on both X (O-L) and Y (R-D).

- Route O-R-D:
  - This route has the highest initial fixed cost (210) but only one variable segment (R-D), making it potentially less costly if fewer participants end up choosing R-D.

**Considering Strategy:**
- The key point to exploit is the dependency on other drivers choosing the same segments. 
- Routes with greater flexibility or fewer variable segments could prove advantageous if they avoid potential bottlenecks.

**Decision:**
Choosing the route O-R-D could be advantageous due to its fixed nature on segment O-R. While it has a high initial fixed cost, if fewer choose R-D, it can become the least costly due to only one increasing segment cost (10Y). Additionally, given the nature of human decisions to cluster around seemingly ‘optimally’ balanced costs, diverging from the majority choosing variable cost routes could become cost-effective over time.

Thus, based on this analysis:

```json
{
  "route": "O-R-D"
}
```

Human: You are agent 11.
Summary of previous round:
  Your Choice: O-R-D
  Route Choice Distribution: {'O-R-D': 12, 'O-L-D': 1, 'O-L-R-D': 5}
  Your Payoff: 20


Human: The available routes are: O-L-D, O-L-R-D, O-R-D.
Think step-by-step before making your decision.

LLM Output: To make a decision for the current round, let's analyze the distribution of choices and the corresponding costs from the previous round.

**Previous Round Analysis:**

1. **Route Choice Distribution:**
   - O-R-D: 12 participants
   - O-L-D: 1 participant
   - O-L-R-D: 5 participants

2. **Costs from Previous Round:**
   - Route O-R-D had 12 participants, therefore the cost was \(210 + 10 \times 12 = 330\).
     - Payoff for choosing O-R-D: \(400 - 330 = 70\).
   - Route O-L-R-D had 5 participants for O-L and 12 participants (since it joins at R) for R-D.
     - Cost for O-L segment: \(10 \times 5 = 50\), cost for R-D: \(10 \times 12 = 120\).
     - Total cost: \(50 + 0 + 120 = 170\).
     - Payoff for choosing O-L-R-D: \(400 - 170 = 230\).
   - Route O-L-D had 1 participant, cost was \(10 \times 1 + 210 = 220\).
     - Payoff for choosing O-L-D: \(400 - 220 = 180\).

**Discussion:**
- In the last round, the majority chose O-R-D, leading to a high cost per participant due to the number of drivers on the segment R-D.
- O-L-R-D and O-L-D had fewer participants, leading to better payoffs.
  
**Decision-making Strategy:**
- Given that O-R-D was a popular choice, it became expensive. Often, fewer participants on less popular routes can yield higher payoffs.
- O-L-D had the least participants, resulting in a decent payoff of 180, second only to O-L-R-D's payoff.
- O-L-R-D offered the greatest payoff due to low numbers at segment O-L and separation before R-D.

**Recommendation:** Consider choosing the less populated route that offers the greatest payoff potential. Given the previous outcome, O-L-R-D provided a high payoff despite having the lower frequency of participants. This choice can potentially maximize payoff if the distribution remains similar or if fewer participants switch to this route. 

Therefore, the strategy would be to move away from the clumping behavior on O-R-D and consider the benefits of choosing O-L-R-D.

Here is the decision based on this analysis:

```json
{
  "route": "O-L-R-D"
}
```

Think step-by-step before making your decision.

LLM Output: To determine the optimal route for the current round, let's analyze the outcome from the previous round and consider a strategy to optimize the payoffs.

**Previous Round Analysis:**

1. **Route Choice Distribution:**
   - O-L-D: 16 participants
   - O-L-R-D: 2 participants
   - O-R-D: 0 participants

2. **Costs from Previous Round:**
   - **O-L-D:** 
     - Cost for O-L segment: \(10 \times 16 = 160\)
     - Total cost: \(160 + 210 = 370\) 
     - Payoff for choosing O-L-D \(400 - 370 = 30\).
   - **O-L-R-D:** 
     - Cost for O-L segment: \(10 \times 2 = 20\)
     - Cost for R-D segment is negligible since no one chose O-R-D.
     - Total cost: \(20 + 0 = 20\)
     - Payoff for choosing O-L-R-D: \(400 - 20 = 380\).
   - **O-R-D:** 
     - Not chosen in the previous round.

**Discussion:**
- The majority had chosen O-L-D, resulting in a very high cost due to heavy congestion on the segment O-L.
- O-L-R-D had very few participants (2), leading to a minimal cost, hence a high payoff.
- The route O-R-D wasn't chosen; had someone chosen it, the fixed costs initially seemed deterring but could be less costly if others start shifting there.

**Strategic Consideration:**
- Choosing O-L-R-D yielded a high payoff in the previous round due to low participation on both O-L and zero influence from R-D.
- O-R-D might not have been considered due to its initial fixed cost and previous popularity, but if some shift here, it could balance costs.

**Decision Recommendation:**
- Staying with O-L-R-D is likely to continue yielding a high payoff if the participation remains low.
- However, keep an eye on O-R-D, it might provide a safe strategy if others start concentrating on O-L-D. 

Given the last round’s high payoff from O-L-R-D and the current distribution, continuing with O-L-R-D could be beneficial as it presented minimal congestion cost.

Here is the decision:

```json
{
  "route": "O-L-R-D"
}
```

- O-L-R-D remains the safer lower-cost choice as it showed a significantly improved payoff compared to O-R-D.

System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 2 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 2 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
If you happen to be the only driver who chooses route O-L-D, and all other 17 drivers choose route O-R-D, then your travel cost from point O to point D is equal to (10 x 1) + 210 = 220.
If, on another round, you and 2 more drivers choose route O-R-D and 15 other drivers choose route O-L-D, then your travel cost for that round will be 210 + (10 x 3) = 240.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```


Human: The available routes are: O-L-D, O-R-D.
Think step-by-step before making your decision.

LLM Output: To decide on the optimal route, let's analyze the situation and consider the potential costs and strategic implications of each choice.

**Route Options and Cost Analysis:**

1. **Route O-L-D:**
   - **Cost Calculation:** \(10X + 210\)
   - **Factors to Consider:**
     - If fewer drivers choose this route, the cost can be relatively low.
     - The cost is variable and depends on how many participants decide on this route.
     - More participants make it costly due to the segment O-L being variable costs proportionate to traffic.

2. **Route O-R-D:**
   - **Cost Calculation:** \(210 + 10Y\)
   - **Factors to Consider:**
     - This route has a fixed initial cost but increases with more participants on R-D.
     - Potentially expensive if many choose it, due to adding variable costs from R-D proportional to participation.

**Strategic Consideration:**

- **Participant Trends:** Since costs depend heavily on how many join each route, anticipating others' decisions can position you advantageously. If a majority tends toward one route, costs will increase rapidly there.
- **Minimize Costs:** The goal will be to choose the less likely popular route to avoid crowding, thus reducing congestion-related costs.

**Optimal Decision Approach:**

- Choose the route that appears less likely to be selected by the majority based on current game dynamics and historical rounds (if applicable)
  
Given the structure of the problem, a switch to diversify away from a crowded route can yield a better payoff.

System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment L-R, cost function: 0
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 3 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 3 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-L-R-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
Supposing that you choose route O-L-R-D, 3 other drivers choose route O-L-D, and 14 additional drivers choose route O-R-D.
Then, your total travel cost for that period is equal to (10 x 4) + 0 + (10 x 14) = 180.
Note that in this example, 4 drivers (including you) traveled on the segment O-L and 14 drivers (again, including you) traveled the segment R-D to go from O to D.
Each of the 3 drivers choosing route O-L-D will be charged a travel cost of (10 x 4) + 210 = 250.
Each of the 14 drivers choosing the route O-R-D will be charged a travel cost of 210 + (10 x 14) = 350.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```


Human: The available routes are: O-L-D, O-L-R-D, O-R-D.
Think step-by-step before making your decision.

LLM Output: To strategically decide on the best route, let's carefully analyze the potential costs for each route and predict participant distribution to minimize costs and maximize payoff.

**Route Options and Cost Analysis:**

1. **Route O-L-D:**
   - **Cost Calculation:** \(10X + 210\), where X is the number of participants choosing segment O-L.
   - If fewer participants choose this, the cost is primarily \(210 + 10 \times X\).
   - High participation leads to increased costs due to congestion on segment O-L.

2. **Route O-L-R-D:**
   - **Cost Calculation:** \(10X + 0 + 10Y\), where X is the number of participants on O-L and Y is on R-D.
   - Free passage on segment L-R.
   - Can become costly if congestion increases significantly on O-L or R-D.

3. **Route O-R-D:**
   - **Cost Calculation:** \(210 + 10Y\), where Y is the number of participants choosing segment R-D.
   - Starts with a fixed cost of 210 for O-R segment.
   - Increased cost if the majority choose this route due to congestion on R-D.

**Strategic Considerations:**

- Predict potential shifts among participants towards less congested routes.
- A focus on balancing participants across routes typically results in minimized costs.
- Historically unused or minimally used routes offer a chance for lower travel costs.
  
**Optimal Decision Approach:**

- Consider O-L-R-D if it consistently offers minimal congestion due to the flexibility of bypassing heavy O-L or R-D segments comparatively.
- If O-R-D has been avoided previously, it might present a low-cost path though care needs to be taken if many participants suddenly switch here.
- Expect that participant behavior will gravitate away from highly congested routes based on previous strategies.

Considering these analyses, choosing a route that balances lower expected congestion will help maximize your payoff.

Here is the decision:

```json
{
  "route": "O-L-R-D"
}
```

     - Cost = \(10 \times 4 + 0 + 10 \times 0 = 40\)
     - Payoff = \(400 - 40 = 360\)
   - **O-R-D:**
     - Not chosen, suggesting it may offer minimal congestion costs if selected.

**Observations:**

- **O-L-D** experienced high congestion, resulting in significant costs and a reduced payoff.
- **O-L-R-D** had a better payoff with fewer participants, indicating it faced lower congestion.
- **O-R-D** was unchosen, indicating potential for reduced congestion costs if pursued.

**Strategic Considerations:**

1. **Avoid High Congestion Routes:**
   - Avoid **O-L-D** due to high participant numbers last round.
   - **O-L-R-D** performed well but may attract more participants this round.

2. **Anticipate Participant Shifts:**
   - Participants dissatisfied with high costs on **O-L-D** might explore **O-R-D**, given it was unselected last round.
   - Historical trends often show participants moving to options not previously used after experiencing this congestion.

3. **Maximize Payoff:**
   - Select a route assumed to have fewer participants to reduce congestion costs.
   - Understand participant movement patterns to optimize route selection effectively.

**Decision Recommendation:**

Opt for **O-R-D** this round. Its previous lack of selection suggests a potential opportunity for lower congestion costs, providing a strategic opportunity for better payoff as participants adjust from crowded paths.

Here's the decision:

System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 2 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 2 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
If you happen to be the only driver who chooses route O-L-D, and all other 17 drivers choose route O-R-D, then your travel cost from point O to point D is equal to (10 x 1) + 210 = 220.
If, on another round, you and 2 more drivers choose route O-R-D and 15 other drivers choose route O-L-D, then your travel cost for that round will be 210 + (10 x 3) = 240.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```


Human: The available routes are: O-L-D, O-R-D.
Think step-by-step before making your decision.

LLM Output: To make a strategic decision this round, let’s walk through the process step-by-step, analyzing potential costs and anticipating participant behavior to select a route that minimizes costs and maximizes payoff.

**1. Evaluate Route Costs:**

- **O-L-D:**
  - **Cost Calculation:** \(10X + 210\), where X is the number of participants on O-L.
  - **Factors to Consider:**
    - High number of participants on this route will increase costs due to the variable cost component (10 * X).
    - Choose if expected participants are low.

- **O-R-D:**
  - **Cost Calculation:** \(210 + 10Y\), where Y is the number of participants on R-D.
  - **Factors to Consider:**
    - Similar logic where fewer participants equate to reduced costs.
    - If historically fewer participants choose this route, it could be advantageous.

**2. Analyze Last Round’s Trends:**

- Given the repetition of either route having higher congestion, look for the pattern where participants shifted routes.
- If last used routes like O-L-D showed high congestion, consider the potential shift of participants towards the opposite.

**3. Predict Participant Behavior:**

- Participants are likely to shift to less crowded routes to achieve better payoffs.
- Those experiencing high congestion typically gravitate towards what was previously less used.

**4. Choose the Route with Lower Expected Congestion:**

Evaluate past patterns, and make the choice based on which path was less used or newly underutilized:

- If historically O-R-D is repeatedly crowded, and O-L-D shows cycles of lesser use, leaning towards O-L-D could be strategic as others migrate back and forth.
- Consider switching to **O-R-D** if the last rounds suggest a mass shift there was avoided.

**Decision Recommendation:**

Choose based on expected moves after previous experiences. If last route use showed congestion, the switch towards less used O-L-D or back to O-R-D can optimize costs.

Here's my recommended route choice based on minimizing expected congestion:

```json
  "route": "O-R-D"
}
```

     - Payoff = \(400 - 220 = 180\)

**Observations:**

- **O-R-D** was extremely crowded, resulting in exorbitant costs and a low payoff.
- **O-L-D** was scarcely used, yielding much lower costs and a significantly higher payoff.

**Strategic Considerations:**

1. **Avoid High Congestion:**
   - Avoid **O-R-D** due to its high congestion and resultant high costs.
   
2. **Anticipate Participant Movement:**
   - Given the high costs on **O-R-D**, participants are likely to consider switching to **O-L-D** looking for less congestion.
   - Historically, participants shift towards the routes with lower previous use and better payoffs.

3. **Maximize Payoff:**
   - Choose a route with fewer anticipated participants to minimize congestion costs.
   - Predict participant behavior based on previous experiences to guide route selection.

**Decision Strategy:**

Based on last round’s congestion, selecting **O-L-D** this round could offer an advantage as participants adjust away from high-cost routes.

**Recommendation:**

Opt for **O-L-D** as participants are expected to move away from the heavily used **O-R-D**, potentially making **O-L-D** the more cost-effective choice.
